feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\\n527: }\\n528: \\n529: func (sched *Scheduler) evaluateNominatedNode(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedMap {\n723: \t\t\tif _, found := failedAndUnresolvableMap[failedNodeName]; found {\n724: \t\t\t\t// failedAndUnresolvableMap takes precedence over failedMap\n725: \t\t\t\t// note that this only happens if the extender returns the node in both maps\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; !found {\n729: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable, failedMsg)\n730: \t\t\t} else {\n731: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName].AppendReason(failedMsg)\n732: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the required format\n756: \tif len(extenders) == 0 && !fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n757: \t\tresult := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, len(nodes))\n758: \t\tfor i := range nodes {\n759: \t\t\tresult = append(result, framework.NodePluginScores{\n760: \t\t\t\tName:       nodes[i].Node().Name,\n761: \t\t\t\tTotalScore: 1,\n762: \t\t\t})\n763: \t\t}\n764: \t\treturn result, nil\n765: \t}\n766: \n767: \t// Run PreScore plugins.\n768: \tpreScoreStatus := fwk.RunPreScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n769: \tif !preScoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n770: \t\treturn nil, preScoreStatus.AsError()\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// Run the Score plugins.\n774: \tnodesScores, scoreStatus := fwk.RunScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n775: \tif !scoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n776: \t\treturn nil, scoreStatus.AsError()\n777: \t}\n778: \n779: \t// Additional details logged at level 10 if enabled.\n780: \tloggerVTen := logger.V(10)\n781: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n782: \t\tfor _, nodeScore := range nodesScores {\n783: \t\t\tfor _, pluginScore := range nodeScore.Scores {\n784: \t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Plugin scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"plugin\", pluginScore.Name, \"node\", nodeScore.Name, \"score\", pluginScore.Score)\n785: \t\t\t}\n786: \t\t}\n787: \t}\n788: \n789: \tif len(extenders) != 0 && nodes != nil {\n790: \t\t// allNodeExtendersScores has all extenders scores for all nodes.\n791: \t\t// It is keyed with node name.\n792: \t\tallNodeExtendersScores := make(map[string]*framework.NodePluginScores, len(nodes))\n793: \t\tvar mu sync.Mutex\n794: \t\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n795: \t\tfor i := range extenders {\n796: \t\t\tif !extenders[i].IsInterested(pod) {\n797: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n798: \t\t\t}\n799: \t\t\twg.Add(1)\n800: \t\t\tgo func(extIndex int) {\n801: \t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Inc()\n802: \t\t\t\tdefer func() {\n803: \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: \\tcntOfMaxScore := 1\\n871: \\tselectedIndex := 0\\n872: \\t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\\n873: \\tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\\n879: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\\n880: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n881: \\t\\t}\\n882: Missing Event Declaration in Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~386-411\n- **Issue**: No event for ResourceSlice Add/Update (though this is driven by the plugin's needs)\n\n## Why This Is A Bug\n\nThe dynamicresources plugin depends on ResourceSlices to determine:\n1. Which resources are available on each node\n2. How many resources are allocated/free\n3. Whether a pod can be scheduled based on resource availability\n\nWhen a ResourceSlice is created/updated:\n- The plugin reads it via `resourceSliceLister` to build the resource model\n- Pods that were previously unschedulable due to insufficient resources might now be schedulable\n- **BUT**: Without an event handler, the scheduler never knows to re-queue these pods for re-evaluation\n- Result: Pods remain stuck in Unschedulable state indefinitely\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (lines 68-96)\n\n```diff\nconst (\n\t// \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n\t// ...\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (lines 448-492)\n\nAdd a method:\n\n```diff\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlice information is used to check device availability on nodes.\n+\t\t// When a driver provides additional resource availability pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// ... rest of framework.QueueingHintFn {\n+\t// Any change to a ResourceSlice may affect resource availability.\n+\t// Pods waiting on resource availability need to be re-evaluated.\n+\treturn framework.Queue\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug Flow\n\n1. **Pod Arrives Before DRA Driver**:\n   - Pod requests a DRA device via ResourceClaim\n   - Scheduler runs dynamicresources plugin's Prefilter\n   - Plugin calls `resourceSliceLister.List()` → no ResourceSlices exist yet\n   - Plugin returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" → pod goes to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlice**:\n   - Driver creates a ResourceSlice with available resources\n   - Event is posted to the API server\n   - **BUG**: Scheduler has no handler registered for ResourceSlice events\n   - Event is silently dropped (no informer callback)\n   - Unschedulable pod is never re-evaluated\n\n3. **Pod Remains Stuck**:\n   - ResourceSlice exists with available resources\n   - Pod's claim could now be allocated\n   - But scheduler never learned about the ResourceSlice update\n   - Pod stays in Pending/Unschedulable forever\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThe root cause is a missing integration between the informer system and the scheduler's event loop:\n\n1. **The Framework Contract**: When a plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares it cares about an event type (e.g., ResourceSlice), the scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` should register an informer callback for that event.\n\n2. **The Missing Link**:\n   - ResourceSlice is NOT declared in the GVK constants (first bug)\n   - Therefore, it cannot be referenced in EventsToRegister\n   - Even if declared in EventsToRegister, there's no handler case for it (second bug)\n   - Result: ResourceSlice events never reach the scheduler queue\n\n3. **The Fix Is Minimal**:\n   - Add one GVK constant (1 line)\n   - Add one switch case with 6-10 lines of code\n   - Add one optional queueing hint function (3-4 lines)\n   - Total: ~15 lines of code\n\n### Impact\n\n- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod\n- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3289,"cache_read_input_tokens":81418,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3289},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"235e229d-e646-4998-900c-ade6c9aa52f5","uuid":"787f27ed-f4f7-4d9c-9b6a-8f734fbfb027"}

information, pods may become schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// ... rest of events ...\n\t}\n```\n\nAnd add the missing queueing hint function:\n\n```diff\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo) framework.QueueingHintFn {\n+\t// Any change to a ResourceSlice may affect resource availability.\n+\t// Pods waiting on resource availability need to be re-evaluated.\n+\treturn framework.Queue\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug Flow\n\n1. **Pod Arrives Before DRA Driver**:\n   - Pod requests a DRA device via ResourceClaim\n   - Scheduler runs dynamicresources plugin's Prefilter\n   - Plugin calls `resourceSliceLister.List()` → no ResourceSlices exist yet\n   - Plugin returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" → pod goes to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlice**:\n   - Driver creates a ResourceSlice with available resources\n   - Event is posted to the API server\n   - **BUG**: Scheduler has no handler registered for ResourceSlice events\n   - Event is silently dropped (no informer callback)\n   - Unschedulable pod is never re-evaluated\n\n3. **Pod Remains Stuck**:\n   - ResourceSlice exists with available resources\n   - Pod's claim could now be allocated\n   - But scheduler never learned about the ResourceSlice update\n   - Pod stays in Pending/Unschedulable forever\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThe root cause is a missing integration between the informer system and the scheduler's event loop:\n\n1. **The Framework Contract**: When a plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares it cares about an event type (e.g., ResourceSlice), the scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` should register an informer callback for that event.\n\n2. **The Missing Link**:\n   - ResourceSlice is NOT declared in the GVK constants (first bug)\n   - Therefore, it cannot be referenced in EventsToRegister\n   - Even if declared in EventsToRegister, there's no handler case for it (second bug)\n   - Result: ResourceSlice events never reach the scheduler queue\n\n3. **The Fix Is Minimal**:\n   - Add one GVK constant (1 line)\n   - Add one switch case with 6-10 lines of code\n   - Add one optional queueing hint function (3-4 lines)\n   - Total: ~15 lines of code\n\n### Impact\n\n- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod\n- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

When Dynamic Resource Allocation drivers publish ResourceSlice objects with available resources, the scheduler is never notified because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue.\n\n**The fix requires:**\n1. Add `ResourceSlice` GVK constant (1 line)\n2. Add ResourceSlice case in `addAllEventHandlers()` switch (8 lines)\n3. Optionally add ResourceSlice to plugin's `EventsToRegister()` (5 lines)\n\n**Result:** Pods requesting DRA resources will be properly re-evaluated when ResourceSlices become available, instead of remaining permanently stuck in Unschedulable state.","originalFile":"# Kubernetes Scheduler ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug Investigation\n\n## Files Examined\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point for scheduling cycle\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Event handler registration mechanism for all cluster events\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — GVK constants for all tracked resource types\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin implementation and EventsToRegister\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/resourceslice.go` — ResourceSlice informer factory\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go` — Resource model building from ResourceSlices\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` (ScheduleOne function, line 66-134)\n   - Pod scheduling occurs, fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod is added to unschedulable queue\n   - No re-evaluation happens when ResourceSlices are created\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (scheduler initialization)\n   - Calls `addAllEventHandlers()` to register event handlers for resource changes\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (addAllEventHandlers function, line 285-546)\n   - Registers event handlers for multiple resource types via a gvkMap switch statement (lines 395-543)\n   - **MISSING**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the switch statement\n   - Covers: CSINode, CSIDriver, CSIStorageCapacity, PersistentVolume, PersistentVolumeClaim, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, StorageClass\n\n4. **Framework issue in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (GVK constants, lines 68-106)\n   - **MISSING**: No `ResourceSlice` GVK constant defined\n   - ResourceSlices are used by the dynamicresources plugin but not declared as a trackable event resource\n\n5. **Resource model built in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (Prefilter method, line 958)\n   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` which loads all ResourceSlices\n   - When a ResourceSlice is added/updated, this model should be invalidated and pods re-evaluated\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Two missing pieces that prevent ResourceSlice events from triggering pod re-evaluation:**\n\n### 1. Missing GVK Constant\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Function**: Constants section\n- **Line**: Should be around line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)\n- **Issue**: ResourceSlice GVK constant is not defined, so the framework doesn't know about this resource type\n\n### 2. Missing Event Handler Registration\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Line**: ~448-492 (the switch statement that handles all gvk cases)\n- **Issue**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the gvkMap switch statement\n  - The switch iterates through gvkMap (which comes from plugins' EventsToRegister)\n  - When ResourceSlice is NOT in gvkMap, it never gets an event handler registered\n  - Therefore, when a ResourceSlice is created/updated, the scheduler is never notified\n\n### 3. Missing Event Declaration in Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~386-411\n- **Issue**: No event for ResourceSlice Add/Update (though this is driven by the plugin's needs)\n\n## Why This Is A Bug\n\nThe dynamicresources plugin depends on ResourceSlices to determine:\n1. Which resources are available on each node\n2. How many resources are allocated/free\n3. Whether a pod can be scheduled based on resource availability\n\nWhen a ResourceSlice is created/updated:\n- The plugin reads it via `resourceSliceLister` to build the resource model\n- Pods that were previously unschedulable due to insufficient resources might now be schedulable\n- **BUT**: Without an event handler, the scheduler never knows to re-queue these pods for re-evaluation\n- Result: Pods remain stuck in Unschedulable state indefinitely\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (lines 68-96)\n\n```diff\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n\tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n\t// ...\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (lines 448-492)\n\nAdd a new case in the gvkMap switch statement in `addAllEventHandlers()`:\n\n```diff\n\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t}\n+\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t}\n\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t// ... existing code ...\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice to EventsToRegister (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (lines 386-412)\n\nAdd ResourceSlice events to the EventsToRegister method:\n\n```diff\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlice information is used to check device availability on nodes.\n+\t\t// When a driver provides additional resource availability information, pods may become schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// ... rest of events ...\n\t}\n```\n\nAnd add the missing queueing hint function:\n\n```diff\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo) framework.QueueingHintFn {\n+\t// Any change to a ResourceSlice may affect resource availability.\n+\t// Pods waiting on resource availability need to be re-evaluated.\n+\treturn framework.Queue\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug Flow\n\n1. **Pod Arrives Before DRA Driver**:\n   - Pod requests a DRA device via ResourceClaim\n   - Scheduler runs dynamicresources plugin's Prefilter\n   - Plugin calls `resourceSliceLister.List()` → no ResourceSlices exist yet\n   - Plugin returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" → pod goes to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlice**:\n   - Driver creates a ResourceSlice with available resources\n   - Event is posted to the API server\n   - **BUG**: Scheduler has no handler registered for ResourceSlice events\n   - Event is silently dropped (no informer callback)\n   - Unschedulable pod is never re-evaluated\n\n3. **Pod Remains Stuck**:\n   - ResourceSlice exists with available resources\n   - Pod's claim could now be allocated\n   - But scheduler never learned about the ResourceSlice update\n   - Pod stays in Pending/Unschedulable forever\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThe root cause is a missing integration between the informer system and the scheduler's event loop:\n\n1. **The Framework Contract**: When a plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares it cares about an event type (e.g., ResourceSlice), the scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` should register an informer callback for that event.\n\n2. **The Missing Link**:\n   - ResourceSlice is NOT declared in the GVK constants (first bug)\n   - Therefore, it cannot be referenced in EventsToRegister\n   - Even if declared in EventsToRegister, there's no handler case for it (second bug)\n   - Result: ResourceSlice events never reach the scheduler queue\n\n3. **The Fix Is Minimal**:\n   - Add one GVK constant (1 line)\n   - Add one switch case with 6-10 lines of code\n   - Add one optional queueing hint function (3-4 lines)\n   - Total: ~15 lines of code\n\n### Impact\n\n- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod\n- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":202,"oldLines":3,"newStart":202,"newLines":40,"lines":[" "," - **Without Fix**: I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Kubernetes scheduler bug. Here's a summary of my findings:\n\n## Investigation Summary\n\n**Bug Identified:** Missing ResourceSlice event handler in the Kubernetes scheduler's event-driven re-queuing mechanism.\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe scheduler has **two critical missing pieces** that prevent ResourceSlice creation/update events from triggering pod re-evaluation:\n\n1. **Missing GVK Constant** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`):\n   - No `ResourceSlice` constant defined in the GVK constants section\n   - All other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc.) are defined, but ResourceSlice is missing\n\n2. **Missing Event Handler Registration** (`pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`):\n   - The `addAllEventHandlers()` function has a switch statement that registers event handlers for all tracked resources\n   - No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the switch statement\n   - When the scheduler starts, it never registers a handler for ResourceSlice events\n\n### Why It's A Bug\n\nThe dynamicresources plugin:\n- Reads ResourceSlices via `resourceSliceLister` during Prefilter to check available resources\n- Returns \"cannot allocate\" when no ResourceSlices exist\n- Pods get added to the unschedulable queue\n- When a DRA driver later publishes ResourceSlices with available resources:\n  - **Event posted to API server** ✓\n  - **No scheduler handler registered** ✗ (THE BUG)\n  - Event silently dropped\n  - Pod never re-evaluated\n  - **Pod remains stuck forever**\n\n### The Fix\n\nThree minimal changes (15 lines total):\n\n1.
